class="jsx-2451481379 table-of-contents-container"><section class="jsx-1695500992">Table of contents:<ul class="jsx-1695500992"><li class="jsx-1695500992 toc-entry"><a href="/physics/speed-of-light#what-is-the-speed-of-light-how-fast-is-the-speed-of-light">What is the speed of light? How fast is the speed of light?</a></li><li class="jsx-1695500992 toc-entry"><a href="/physics/speed-of-light#how-to-calculate-the-speed-of-light">How to calculate the speed of light?</a></li><li class="jsx-1695500992 toc-entry"><a href="/physics/speed-of-light#faq">FAQ</a></li></ul></section></div></div></section><div class="jsx-766628155 spacerBottom"></div><div class="jsx-1889808109 CalculatorDetailsDivider"><div class="jsx-1889808109 divider"><hr class="MuiDivider-root"></div></div><div id="calculator-description" class="jsx-766628155"><div class="StyledHtml jsx-3421022985 jsx-1376048448"><div class="contentPart css-5ca4gx"><div class="textBlock"><p>With this speed of light calculator, we aim to help you <strong>calculate the distance light can travel in a fixed time</strong>. As the speed of light is the fastest speed in the universe, it would be fascinating to know just how far it can travel in a short amount of time.</p>
<p>We have written this article to help you understand <strong>what the speed of light is</strong>, <strong>how fast the speed of light is</strong>, and <strong>how to calculate the speed of light</strong>. We will also demonstrate some examples to help you understand the computation of the speed of light.</p></div></div><div class="jsx-1030690091 contentPartPromo"><div><div id="/52555387/omnicalculator.com_300x250_1" style="min-height: 250px; max-height: 250px; overflow: hidden; position: relative;"><div data-pw-desk="med_rect_btf" id="med_rect_btf" class="pw-tag" data-google-query-id="COfxzP-orYIDFdPgcwEdSpEH-w" style="max-height: 261px;"><div id="google_ads_iframe_/154013155,141498546/1024461/73225/publisher:1024461-website:73225-medium_rectangle_0__container__" style="border: 0pt none;"><iframe id="google_ads_iframe_/154013155,141498546/1024461/73225/publisher:1024461-website:73225-medium_rectangle_0" name="google_ads_iframe_/154013155,141498546/1024461/73225/publisher:1024461-website:73225-medium_rectangle_0" title="3rd party ad content" width="300" height="250" scrolling="no" marginwidth="0" marginheight="0" frameborder="0" role="region" aria-label="ad" tabindex="0" sandbox="allow-forms allow-pointer-lock allow-popups allow-popups-to-escape-sandbox allow-same-origin allow-scripts allow-top-navigation-by-user-activation allow-presentation" style="border: 0px; vertical-align: bottom;" data-load-complete="true" data-google-container-id="1"></iframe></div><div class="pw_report_ad_container" style="line-height:normal;display:inline-flex;justify-content:center"><a id="report_ad_med_rect_btf" href="#" class="playwire_report_ad_link" style="color: #4db2ec !important; 
                    font-size:10px !important;
                    font-family:&quot;Open Sans&quot;,arial,sans-serif !important;
                    font-weight: normal !important;
                    font-style: normal !important;
                    text-decoration: none !important;
                ">Report Ad</a></div></div></div></div></div><div class="contentPart css-5ca4gx"><h2 id="what-is-the-speed-of-light-how-fast-is-the-speed-of-light">What is the speed of light? How fast is the speed of light?</h2>
<div class="textBlock"><p>The speed of light is scientifically proven to be the universe's maximum speed. This means no matter how hard you try, you can never exceed this speed in this universe. Hence, there are also some theories on getting into another universe by breaking this limit. You can understand this more using our <a href="/everyday-life/speed" class="js-link">speed calculator</a> and <a href="/math/distance" class="js-link">distance calculator</a>.</p>
<p>So, how fast is the speed of light? The <strong>speed of light is 299,792,458 m/s</strong> in a vacuum. The <strong>speed of light in mph is 670,616,629 mph</strong>. With this speed, one can go around the globe more than 400,000 times in a minute!</p>
<p>One thing to note is that the speed of light slows down when it goes through different mediums. Light travels faster in air than in water, for instance. This phenomenon causes the refraction of light.</p>
<p>Now, let's look at how to calculate the speed of light.</p></div></div><div class="contentPart css-5ca4gx"><h2 id="how-to-calculate-the-speed-of-light">How to calculate the speed of light?</h2>
<div class="textBlock"><p>As the speed of light is constant, calculating the speed of light usually falls on calculating the distance that light can travel in a certain time period. Hence, let's have a look at the following example:</p>
<ul>
<li>Source: Light</li>
<li>Speed of light: 299,792,458 m/s</li>
<li>Time traveled: 100 seconds</li>
</ul>
<p>You can perform the calculation in three steps:</p>
<ol>
<li>
<p><strong>Determine the speed of light.</strong></p>
<p>As mentioned, the speed of light is the fastest speed in the universe, and it is always a constant in a vacuum. Hence, the <code>speed of light</code> is <code>299,792,458 m/s</code>.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p><strong>Determine the time that the light has traveled.</strong></p>
<p>The next step is to know how much time the light has traveled. Unlike looking at the speed of a sports car or a train, the speed of light is extremely fast, so the time interval that we look at is usually measured in seconds instead of minutes and hours. You can use our <a href="/other/time-lapse" class="js-link">time lapse calculator</a> to help you with this calculation.</p>
<p>For this example, the <code>time</code> that the light has traveled is <code>100 seconds</code>.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p><strong>Calculate the distance that the light has traveled.</strong></p>
<p>The final step is to calculate the total distance that the light has traveled within the <code>time</code>. You can calculate this answer using the speed of light formula:</p>
<p><code>distance = speed of light × time</code></p>
<p>Thus, the <code>distance</code> that the light can travel in <code>100 seconds</code> is <code>299,792,458 m/s × 100 seconds = 29,979,245,800 m</code></p>
</li>
</ol></div></div><div class="contentPart css-5ca4gx"><h2 id="faq">FAQ</h2>
<h3>What is the speed of light in mph when it is in a vacuum?</h3><div class="textBlock"><p>The <strong>speed of light in a vacuum is <code>670,616,629</code> mph</strong>. This is equivalent to <code>299,792,458</code> m/s or <code>1,079,252,849</code> km/h. This is the fastest speed in the universe.</p></div></div><div class="contentPart css-5ca4gx"><h3>Is the speed of light always constant?</h3><div class="textBlock"><p><strong>Yes</strong>, the speed of light is always constant for a given medium. The speed of light changes when going through different mediums. For example, light travels slower in water than in air.</p></div></div><div class="contentPart css-5ca4gx"><h3>How can I calculate the speed of light?</h3><div class="textBlock"><p>You can calculate the speed of light in three steps:</p>
<ol>
<li>
<p>Determine the <strong>time</strong> that the light has traveled.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Determine the <strong>distance</strong> the light has traveled.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Apply the <strong>speed of light formula</strong>:</p>
<p><code>speed of light = distance / time</code></p>
</li>
</ol></div></div><div class="contentPart css-5ca4gx"><h3>How far can the speed of light travel in 1 minute?</h3><div class="textBlock"><p>Light <strong>can travel <code>17,987,547,480 m</code> in 1 minute</strong>. This means that light can travel around the earth more than <code>448</code> times in a minute.</p></div></div></div></div><div class="jsx-2831992045 plain-variant"><div class="jsx-2831992045"><span class="jsx-4037849880 ">Wei Bin Loo</span></div><div class="jsx-2831992045"></div><div class="jsx-2831992045"></div></div><div class="jsx-766628155 spacerBottom"></div></div><div class="jsx-2269565380
